Data = read.table(textConnection(Input),header=TRUE)

###  Order factors by the order in data frame
###  Otherwise, R will alphabetize them

Data$treatment = factor(Data$treatment,
                        levels=unique(Data$treatment))

Data$metatranscriptome       = factor(Data$metatranscriptome,
                                      levels=unique(Data$metatranscriptome))


###  Check the data frame

library(psych)
headTail(Data)
str(Data)
summary(Data)   

### Remove unnecessary objects

rm(Input)

#In this first example, the model will be specified with the lmer function 
#in the package lme4.  The term (1|Town) in the model formula indicates that 
#Town should be treated as a random variable, with each level having its own 
#in the model.  The anova function in the package lmerTest is used to 
#produce p-values for the fixed effects.  The rand function in the package 
#lmerTest produces p-values for the random effects. 

library(lme4)
library(lmerTest)
##### here I use time as random effect
#### model = lmer(VOC_log2 ~ Treatment + (1|Plot_ID) +(1|Time),
### data=Data,
####REML=TRUE)


model = lmer(rank ~ treatment + (1|metatranscriptome),
             data=Data,
             REML=TRUE)

anova(model)
rand(model)

summary(model)

###  Order factors by the order in data frame
###  Otherwise, R will alphabetize them

Data$treatment = factor(Data$treatment,
                        levels=unique(Data$treatment))

                                      levels=unique(Data$metatranscriptome))


###  Check the data frame

library(psych)
headTail(Data)
str(Data)
summary(Data)   

### Remove unnecessary objects

rm(Input)

#In this first example, the model will be specified with the lmer function 
#in the package lme4.  The term (1|Town) in the model formula indicates that 
#Town should be treated as a random variable, with each level having its own 
#in the model.  The anova function in the package lmerTest is used to 
#produce p-values for the fixed effects.  The rand function in the package 
#lmerTest produces p-values for the random effects. 

library(lme4)
library(lmerTest)
##### here I use time as random effect
#### model = lmer(VOC_log2 ~ Treatment + (1|Plot_ID) +(1|Time),
### data=Data,
####REML=TRUE)


model = lmer(rank ~ treatment + (1|metatranscriptome),
             data=Data,
             REML=TRUE)

anova(model)
rand(model)

summary(model)

Data = read.table(textConnection(Input),header=TRUE)

###  Order factors by the order in data frame
###  Otherwise, R will alphabetize them

Data$treatment = factor(Data$treatment,
                        levels=unique(Data$treatment))

Data$metatranscriptome       = factor(Data$metatranscriptome,
                                      levels=unique(Data$metatranscriptome))


###  Check the data frame

library(psych)
headTail(Data)
str(Data)
summary(Data)   

### Remove unnecessary objects

rm(Input)

#In this first example, the model will be specified with the lmer function 
#in the package lme4.  The term (1|Town) in the model formula indicates that 
#Town should be treated as a random variable, with each level having its own 
#in the model.  The anova function in the package lmerTest is used to 
#produce p-values for the fixed effects.  The rand function in the package 
#lmerTest produces p-values for the random effects. 

library(lme4)
library(lmerTest)
##### here I use time as random effect
#### model = lmer(VOC_log2 ~ Treatment + (1|Plot_ID) +(1|Time),
### data=Data,
####REML=TRUE)


model = lmer(rank ~ treatment + (1|metatranscriptome),
             data=Data,
             REML=TRUE)

anova(model)
rand(model)

summary(model)

Data = read.table(textConnection(Input),header=TRUE)

###  Order factors by the order in data frame
###  Otherwise, R will alphabetize them

Data$treatment = factor(Data$treatment,
                        levels=unique(Data$treatment))

Data$metatranscriptome       = factor(Data$metatranscriptome,
                                      levels=unique(Data$metatranscriptome))


###  Check the data frame

library(psych)
headTail(Data)
str(Data)
summary(Data)   

### Remove unnecessary objects

rm(Input)

#In this first example, the model will be specified with the lmer function 
#in the package lme4.  The term (1|Town) in the model formula indicates that 
#Town should be treated as a random variable, with each level having its own 
#in the model.  The anova function in the package lmerTest is used to 
#produce p-values for the fixed effects.  The rand function in the package 
#lmerTest produces p-values for the random effects. 

library(lme4)
library(lmerTest)
##### here I use time as random effect
#### model = lmer(VOC_log2 ~ Treatment + (1|Plot_ID) +(1|Time),
### data=Data,
####REML=TRUE)


model = lmer(rank ~ treatment + (1|metatranscriptome),
             data=Data,
             REML=TRUE)

anova(model)
rand(model)

summary(model)

                        levels=unique(Data$treatment))

                                      levels=unique(Data$metatranscriptome))

headTail(Data)
str(Data)
summary(Data)   

### Remove unnecessary objects

rm(Input)

#In this first example, the model will be specified with the lmer function 
#in the package lme4.  The term (1|Town) in the model formula indicates that 
#Town should be treated as a random variable, with each level having its own 
#in the model.  The anova function in the package lmerTest is used to 
#produce p-values for the fixed effects.  The rand function in the package 
#lmerTest produces p-values for the random effects. 

library(lme4)
library(lmerTest)
##### here I use time as random effect
#### model = lmer(VOC_log2 ~ Treatment + (1|Plot_ID) +(1|Time),
### data=Data,
####REML=TRUE)


model = lmer(rank ~ treatment + (1|metatranscriptome),
             data=Data,
             REML=TRUE)

anova(model)
rand(model)

summary(model)

#In this first example, the model will be specified with the lmer function 
#in the package lme4.  The term (1|Town) in the model formula indicates that 
#Town should be treated as a random variable, with each level having its own 
#in the model.  The anova function in the package lmerTest is used to 
#produce p-values for the fixed effects.  The rand function in the package 
#lmerTest produces p-values for the random effects. 

library(lme4)
library(lmerTest)
##### here I use time as random effect
#### model = lmer(VOC_log2 ~ Treatment + (1|Plot_ID) +(1|Time),
### data=Data,
####REML=TRUE)


model = lmer(rank ~ treatment + (1|metatranscriptome),
             data=Data,
             REML=TRUE)

anova(model)
rand(model)

summary(model)

#In this first example, the model will be specified with the lmer function 
#in the package lme4.  The term (1|Town) in the model formula indicates that 
#Town should be treated as a random variable, with each level having its own 
#in the model.  The anova function in the package lmerTest is used to 
#produce p-values for the fixed effects.  The rand function in the package 
#lmerTest produces p-values for the random effects. 

library(lme4)
library(lmerTest)
##### here I use time as random effect
#### model = lmer(VOC_log2 ~ Treatment + (1|Plot_ID) +(1|Time),
### data=Data,
####REML=TRUE)


model = lmer(rank ~ species + (1|metatranscriptome),
             data=Data,
             REML=TRUE)

anova(model)
rand(model)

summary(model)

#produce p-values for the fixed effects.  The rand function in the package 
#lmerTest produces p-values for the random effects. 

library(lme4)
library(lmerTest)
##### here I use time as random effect
#### model = lmer(VOC_log2 ~ Treatment + (1|Plot_ID) +(1|Time),
### data=Data,
####REML=TRUE)


model = lmer(rank ~ species + (1|metatranscriptome),
             data=Data,
             REML=TRUE)

anova(model)
rand(model)

summary(model)

Data = read.table(textConnection(Input),header=TRUE)

###  Order factors by the order in data frame
###  Otherwise, R will alphabetize them

Data$species = factor(Data$species,
                      levels=unique(Data$species))

Data$metatranscriptome       = factor(Data$metatranscriptome,
                                      levels=unique(Data$metatranscriptome))


###  Check the data frame

library(psych)
headTail(Data)
str(Data)
summary(Data)   

### Remove unnecessary objects

rm(Input)

#In this first example, the model will be specified with the lmer function 
#in the package lme4.  The term (1|Town) in the model formula indicates that 
#Town should be treated as a random variable, with each level having its own 
#in the model.  The anova function in the package lmerTest is used to 
#produce p-values for the fixed effects.  The rand function in the package 
#lmerTest produces p-values for the random effects. 

library(lme4)
library(lmerTest)
##### here I use time as random effect
#### model = lmer(VOC_log2 ~ Treatment + (1|Plot_ID) +(1|Time),
### data=Data,
####REML=TRUE)


model = lmer(rank ~ species + (1|metatranscriptome),
             data=Data,
             REML=TRUE)

anova(model)
rand(model)

summary(model)

#In this first example, the model will be specified with the lmer function 
#in the package lme4.  The term (1|Town) in the model formula indicates that 
#Town should be treated as a random variable, with each level having its own 
#in the model.  The anova function in the package lmerTest is used to 
#produce p-values for the fixed effects.  The rand function in the package 
#lmerTest produces p-values for the random effects.

library(lmerTest)
##### here I use time as random effect
#### model = lmer(VOC_log2 ~ Treatment + (1|Plot_ID) +(1|Time),
### data=Data,
####REML=TRUE)

             data=Data,
             REML=TRUE)

#In this first example, the model will be specified with the lmer function 
#in the package lme4.  The term (1|Town) in the model formula indicates that 
#Town should be treated as a random variable, with each level having its own 
#in the model.  The anova function in the package lmerTest is used to 
#produce p-values for the fixed effects.  The rand function in the package 
#lmerTest produces p-values for the random effects. 

library(lme4)
library(lmerTest)
##### here I use time as random effect
#### model = lmer(VOC_log2 ~ Treatment + (1|Plot_ID) +(1|Time),
### data=Data,
####REML=TRUE)


model = lmer(rank ~ species + (1|metatranscriptome),
             data=Data,
             REML=TRUE)

anova(model)
rand(model)

summary(model)

Data = read.table(textConnection(Input),header=TRUE)

rank_control <- c(Data$M_up)  
rank_warmed <- c(Data$P_up)

t.test(rank_control,rank_warmed,paired=FALSE)
